    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->Nirmal Kumar is a professionally qualified and experienced Executive and Team coach who:<!----><br><!---->1.	is a seasoned veteran having coached scores of executives, business owners over 5 years to attain their business and personal goals<!----><br><!---->2.	follows a World class proven methodology used by Fortune 500 companies– the Marshall Goldsmith Stakeholder Centered Coaching (MGSCC) methodology<span class="white-space-pre"> </span><br><!---->3.	is a Marshall Goldsmith Certified Executive and Team Coach<span class="white-space-pre"> </span><br><!---->4.	is a Global Coach Group Certified Executive and Team Coach<span class="white-space-pre"> </span><br><!---->5.	is a Certified Global Leadership Assessment Professional<span class="white-space-pre"> </span><br><!---->6.	has helped enhance the Spiritual Quotient (SQ) of over 75 individuals as a Counselor and Coach, over 15 years in an International Spiritual Organization present in most countries in the world<!----><br><!---->7.	uses the Global Leadership Assessment Tool GLA 360 to assess team and members’ performance<!----><br><!---->8.	uses the latest technology to help teams and leaders perform better<!----><br><!---->9.	guarantees measurable leadership growth<!----><br><!---->10.	has been a Learning Facilitator to hundreds of executives of top companies and Banks, in India and abroad<!----><br><!---->11.	has extensive experience having worked for over 4 decades in Management and Leadership in different verticals<!----><br><!---->12.	has worked as a member on international Tech Teams<!----><br></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->Nirmal Kumar is a professionally qualified and experienced Executive and Team coach who:

          <li style="width: 451px; max-width: none; min-width: auto;" data-item-index="1" id="ember99" class="artdeco-carousel__item ember-view"><div data-test-display="display" class="artdeco-carousel__item-container">

      <div class="pvs-content__top-bar">
          <div class="mt3 mb2 mh3 display-flex t-12 t-black--light display-flex t-normal">
            <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->Published · 7yr<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->Published · 7yr<!----></span>
          </div>
      </div>
<!---->  </a>

          <a class="optional-action-target-wrapper flex-1 display-flex full-width relative
      " target="_self" href="https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/lets-get-life-back-work-life-balance-nirmal-kumar">
        <div class="display-flex flex-column full-width">
      <div class="pvs-media-content__image-wrapper">
        <div class="pvs-media-content__image-aspect-ratio">
          <div class="ivm-image-view-model   " id="content-image-ember100">
    <div class="ivm-view-attr__img-wrapper ivm-view-attr__img-wrapper--use-img-tag display-flex
    
    ">
<!---->      <img width="400" src="https://media-exp1.licdn.com/dms/image/C5612AQGDts9N63rgQA/article-cover_image-shrink_600_2000/0/1520151287065?e=1650499200&amp;v=beta&amp;t=-kuF_hJ33b0WGO96uowon8nczMRsrmby_Jx0OZ1tZoM" loading="lazy" height="400" alt="Image for Let's get 'Life' back into the 'Work-Life' Balance" id="ember101" class="ivm-view-attr__img--centered pvs-media-content__image lazy-image ember-view">
</div>
  </div>
        </div>
      </div>
      <div class="pvs-media-content__preview">
          <div class="mb1">
              <div class="display-flex ">
    <div class="display-flex full-width">
    
      
  <div class="pv-shared-text-with-see-more t-14 t-black t-bold break-words display-flex align-items-center">
    <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
    " style="line-height:1.9rem;max-height:3.8rem;-webkit-line-clamp:2;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->Let's get 'Life' back into the 'Work-Life' Balance<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->Let's get 'Life' back into the 'Work-Life' Balance<!----></span>

<!----></div>
  </div>

  
  </div>

</div>
              <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
     t-12 t-black--light t-normal break-words" style="line-height:1.5rem;max-height:1.5rem;-webkit-line-clamp:1;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->Nirmal Kumar<!----><span class="white-space-pre"> </span>on LinkedIn<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->Nirmal Kumar<!----><span class="white-space-pre"> </span>on LinkedIn<!----></span>

<!----></div>
          </div>
          <div class="display-flex ">
    <div class="display-flex full-width">
    
      
  <div class="pv-shared-text-with-see-more text-body-small break-words display-flex align-items-center">
    <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
    " style="line-height:1.9rem;max-height:11.399999999999999rem;-webkit-line-clamp:6;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->The good ol' days: It was the late 1970s. I was working in a Government owned Bank in India. There were no computers then. All books of accounts (Ledgers) were to be tallied and balanced manually. During the half yearly and annual book closings it would require quite a bit of extra work to balance the books in time for the next accounting period. The process would involve overtime payments to the staff. The employees looked forward to the additional cash every half year, although it meant extra work! The employees would work extra hours and would also help each other when required. Weekends and holidays were time for the staff to enjoy work as a team together! There were never any complaints of 'Work-Life Balance' or "Work stress". The hectic pace of dotcoms Cut to the year 2000. Companies are getting on to the dotcom bandwagon and are trying to differentiate themselves. Quality certifications are very much sought after. I am now working in an IT company that develops software applications for the Banking sector. One of my colleagues is the Management Representative (MR) for the IT Company's initiative to get an ISO certification. He works day and night for getting the documentation in order. On D-day, just hours before the certification agency's auditors were to arrive at the office, the MR vomits blood and collapses on the office premises. At the hospital, he is declared 'dead on arrival'. His work-life balance had gone for a toss. Stress claimed a victim! In both cases, the management and employees had mutually agreed expectations. The employees had committed themselves to meet the expectations. They were being adequately compensated. What had happened in 20 years that had so drastically changed our lives? A quick contemplation and the following 3 factors come to mind: Nature of knowledge work: Certain industries like the IT industry, by the very nature of the work, put pressure on the thinking faculties of employees. They do not have to just follow procedures as in the operations section of the Banking industry. They have to create new functionalities, modules and programs to survive. Processes are weak. Dependence on people is high. Competitiveness squeezes the workforce. Market economics: There are high expectations on the sunrise industries like Information Technology, biotech, and so on. This translates into high stress in employees. Profits have to justify the capital market expectations. The speed of change: I remember reading about the new 'Information Superhighway' as the internet was called in the latter half of the 90s decade. When email was first introduced there was a pressure to respond quickly. No longer did we have the luxury of deliberating on what we wanted to communicate. There was a sense of urgency in everything we did. During the industrial revolution the physical movement of the assembly line determined the speed of business. With the coming of the internet, business now happened ‘at the speed of thought’. The speed of change also pushed many jobs out of the market and introduced newer ones. There was a churn. And as with every strategic inflection point there was huge stress on everyone! The last few years With the widespread use of mobile phones and social media we have information being generated by millions of people every second. Our human capacity to process and consume information is limited. We need search engines to decide for us. We are now facing an information overload which has strongly impacted our attention span. We now have a double whammy: The internet creating huge stress and portable devices creating attention related disorders. How do we protect ourselves? We can start by taking back control of our lives. Only we can decide what we want should be in our lives. We need to be choosy. After all it’s our life. We need to resist the seductive pull of technology, of always being online, on top of things! We will not be left behind if we are not aware of the latest trends, which change by the hour anyway! We need to have a life outside of technology, a life where we connect with our inner selves and our real priorities in life, really (not virtually) relate with people who are important to us, and focus on the contribution we can make to the real world we live in. Only then can we say we have a life and only then can we have balance! (The author is the Founder and Principal Consultant at ELM Consultancy and can be reached at nirmal@elmconsultancy.com. ELM Consultancy specializes in providing insights and solutions for individuals and employees to promote Excellence in Leadership and Management (ELM). To subscribe to his blog please click http://www.elmconsultancy.com/subscribe-to-blog.html)<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->The good ol' days: It was the late 1970s. I was working in a Government owned Bank in India. There were no computers then. All books of accounts (Ledgers) were to be tallied and balanced manually. <!---->      <img width="400" src="https://media-exp1.licdn.com/dms/image/C5612AQGv_cWMwpJWNQ/article-cover_image-shrink_600_2000/0/1520234055192?e=1650499200&amp;v=beta&amp;t=U-wQEy2l0Rop-na7d_0tHigUjaiL56fjf9RIOwsEup8" loading="lazy" height="400" alt="Image for 5 hints managers give team members ....and how to act on them!" id="ember104" class="ivm-view-attr__img--centered pvs-media-content__image lazy-image ember-view">

      </div>
      <div class="pvs-media-content__preview">
          <div class="mb1">
              <div class="display-flex ">
    <div class="display-flex full-width">
    
      
  <div class="pv-shared-text-with-see-more t-14 t-black t-bold break-words display-flex align-items-center">
    <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
    " style="line-height:1.9rem;max-height:3.8rem;-webkit-line-clamp:2;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->5 hints managers give team members ....and how to act on them!<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->5 hints managers give team members ....and how to act on them!<!----></span>

<!----></div>
  </div>

  
  </div>

</div>
              <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
     t-12 t-black--light t-normal break-words" style="line-height:1.5rem;max-height:1.5rem;-webkit-line-clamp:1;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->Nirmal Kumar<!----><span class="white-space-pre"> </span>on LinkedIn<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->Nirmal Kumar<!----><span class="white-space-pre"> </span>on LinkedIn<!----></span>

<!---->
<!----></div>
          </div>
          <div class="display-flex ">
    <div class="display-flex full-width">
    
      
  <div class="pv-shared-text-with-see-more text-body-small break-words display-flex align-items-center">
    <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
    " style="line-height:1.9rem;max-height:11.399999999999999rem;-webkit-line-clamp:6;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->In a difficult employment scenario with cut throat competition for scarce jobs, getting the right personnel would be easy, right? Wrong! Many managers would prefer to get performance out of the existing employees rather than getting them out of the team. It is far more expensive and time-consuming to recruit and train a new employee. Here are 5 of the common methods managers use to give a veiled message to the employee without really upsetting them. 1. The Sandwich “Congratulations! You are doing a wonderful job on XYZ Project. It is one of our best projects. Only some small things need to be taken care of. Your team is doing well but they come in at all hours and leave when they want. This impacts other projects. You are a good manager and I am sure you could take care of this aspect. We have already seen how XY Z Project is racing towards completion on schedule! Keep up the good work!” The sandwich is usually used when giving a correction to a good performer. The employee is too good to lose, but the message has to be sent across. Praise, correction, praise. That comprises the sandwich! 2. The Sweet Pill “I have to let you know that you are really performing very well on your assigned tasks. The contribution of your team to the overall profitability of the company is commendable. However, this year is particularly tough and even the best managers are having a difficult time proving themselves. I am sure you will come out with flying colors before the year is over!” This is a variation of the Sandwich. The team member is treated very nicely and politely. She is shown all courtesy and respect due to a valuable employee. The message is given so subtly that the team member does not notice until much later! She has to contemplate deeply to understand the message. 3. The Briefing “The company has been going through some turbulent situations in the past 3-4 months. Sales have been flat while expenses are rising. Profits have taken a hit. The Management team needs to introspect deeply and find out the reasons for this mess that we are in. Is it that we are not working hard enough? Are our employees not coming to office on time? Are they taking more leave than planned? What is the cause of this rot? How are we going to get out of this mess? As responsible managers we all need to put our heads into this problem and arrive at a plan of action. We shall meet on Saturday for your inputs and action plans!” More often than not this is a message for a particular manager but delivered in a general way to all managers. If the erring manager does not plan to correct her team by Saturday, other strategies would be put to use! 4. The Capsule This is a variation of the briefing. When the briefing is used with a particular manager or group it assumes the shape of a capsule. The message is given cloaked in the guise of bad circumstances. It is like a gelatin capsule holding the medicine inside. The circumstances may or may not be catastrophic, but the message is subtly pushed down the throats of the non-performing managers. 5. The Squeeze “It has been observed that our employees have been very lax about the usage of facilities and consumables in the office. Papers, clips, pins have been found lying around the office and on the floors, especially near the copiers and printers. All employees are henceforth required to obtain the permission of the General Manager for any issue of stationery and for printing or copying tasks.” This is a not-so-subtle message to the manager that all his powers have been effectively withdrawn. The squeeze is only a strategy to get the manager to speak to the boss and agree with him in some other matter. This is a manipulative move and is sometimes used to give a tough message indirectly. What would you do if you got one of the hints? Trust results in clarity, openness and better communication. When the manager needs to give a hint, it means trust is lacking. Both, the manager and the team member need to work on the relationship. The trust deficit leads to inadequate or imperfect communication, which further increases the trust deficit. The way out of this vicious cycle is to discuss, invest in the relationship and reset expectations. The team member could do well to ask the manager for a discussion on the expectations from her and her team. Assuming the manager is a mature person, she would appreciate the initiative and use the opportunity to rebuild trust! What happens if the team members do not take the hint? The manager then uses several other strategies to get them off the team! But those can wait for another day. Please let me know in the comments below, about more such techniques you have observed managers using! (The author is the Founder and Principal Consultant at ELM Consultancy and can be reached at nirmal@elmconsultancy.com. ELM Consultancy specializes in providing insights and solutions for individuals and employees to promote Excellence in Leadership and Management (ELM). To subscribe to his blog please click http://www.elmconsultancy.com/subscribe-to-blog.html)<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->In a difficult employment scenario with cut throat competition for scarce jobs, getting the right personnel would be easy, right? Wrong! Many managers would prefer to get performance out of the existing employees rather than getting them out of the team. <!---->      <img width="400" src="https://media-exp1.licdn.com/dms/image/C5612AQEjLcM5IU7qYg/article-cover_image-shrink_600_2000/0/1520151644257?e=1650499200&amp;v=beta&amp;t=P6OaZusrtFR0Bcmq9hQwlUNPihQgBLmMyX1rKXU2p3g" loading="lazy" height="400" alt="Image for 10 ways your boss could fire you!     <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->10 ways your boss could fire you! (Part 1)<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->10 ways your boss could fire you! (Part 1)<!----></span>

<!----></div>
  </div>

  
  </div>

</div>
              <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
     t-12 t-black--light t-normal break-words" style="line-height:1.5rem;max-height:1.5rem;-webkit-line-clamp:1;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->Nirmal Kumar<!----><span class="white-space-pre"> </span>on LinkedIn<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->Nirmal Kumar<!----><span class="white-space-pre"> </span>on LinkedIn<!----></span>

<!----></div>
          </div>
          <div class="display-flex ">
    <div class="display-flex full-width">
    
      
  <div class="pv-shared-text-with-see-more text-body-small break-words display-flex align-items-center">
    <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
    " style="line-height:1.9rem;max-height:11.399999999999999rem;-webkit-line-clamp:6;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->In a previous post we had discussed how managers give hints to their subordinates to get them to perform. If the subordinates do not get it, then newer strategies are used. As jobs become scarce and individuals find themselves becoming entrepreneurs more out of compulsion than choice, bosses are using different ways of letting their subordinates go. Here are 10 such techniques: 1. The Guillotine This is standard practice nowadays! You are called into the boss’ cabin around mid day where the HR representative is also present. The boss informs you, with a straight and purportedly compassionate face, that your job has become redundant and that you are being let go. Please sign this document in duplicate. You may keep one copy for your records. Please return all the company’s belongings within an hour. Meanwhile your access card and internet connection have been disabled. You cannot go out or connect with anybody. Once your boss has received all the stuff from you, including the data, you will be escorted out. Everything is done quickly and effectively, like a guillotine. Your head falls into the basket and it’s over. Next! 2. The Barbecue This is still done sometimes! You are at that important meeting where all your peers are assembled. The boss is making his pitch about how the company is in dire straits. The teams are not performing and he names your team as an example. Everyone glances at you from the corner of their eyes. The boss goes on about how the team could do better. You are being hauled over the coals. Not knowing where to look, you stare at your thumbs, absolutely stunned! You know you cannot defend yourself. The boss does not permit it! The meeting is over. You quickly go to your desk and email your resignation. Then you go home avoiding your colleagues! 3. The Public Execution This is a variation of the Barbecue. In the important meeting where all your peers are present, the boss names you directly as the person most responsible for the mess that the company is in. The light from the projector casts a shadow on the screen in front of the presentation showing the company results. It is a rotating shadow of a person. You see your shadow in silhouette as you limply hang from the ceiling. 4. The Assisted Dive You are called into the boss’s cabin for an urgent meeting. The boss says he has a very important assignment for you. It is very challenging but he is confident that you are one of chosen few who could succeed. He needs someone trustworthy and efficient as a partner in shouldering a great responsibility. You have been appointed the head of a division! You realize it is one of the company’s worst performing divisions. The one which you thought was being hived off! Now you have been tasked with turning it around! And of course, you will have the boss’s full support and cooperation! You have been asked to dive into the pool. You will be guided in your dive. Only, there is very little water in the pool! 5. The Bouquet This is another variation of the Assisted Dive. The boss calls you in and congratulates you. You have been given a raise. Your performance has been exceptional and the company is proud of you. He hands you a bouquet. Commensurate with your increased remuneration you now have additional responsibilities of turning around the under-performing department. The boss sends an email to all your peers, congratulating you, informing of your added responsibilities and wishing you all the best. You feel the thorns pricking in your hand as you hold the bouquet tightly! You look down. There is blood on the floor, yours! Well, there are at least 5 more to come. But let’s not have too much negativity in one week! Have you seen the techniques in action? Hopefully being used on someone else! Please leave your comments below. (The author is the Founder and Principal Consultant at ELM Consultancy and can be reached at nirmal@elmconsultancy.com. ELM Consultancy specializes in providing insights and solutions for individuals and employees to promote Excellence in Leadership and Management (ELM).           <div class="mb1">
              <div class="display-flex ">
    <div class="display-flex full-width">
    
      
  <div class="pv-shared-text-with-see-more t-14 t-black t-bold break-words display-flex align-items-center">
    <div class="inline-show-more-text

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->10 ways your boss could fire you! (Part 2)<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->10 ways your boss could fire you! (Part 2)<!----></span>

<!----></div>
  </div>

  
  </div>

</div>
              <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
     t-12 t-black--light t-normal break-words" style="line-height:1.5rem;max-height:1.5rem;-webkit-line-clamp:1;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->Nirmal Kumar<!----><span class="white-space-pre"> </span>on LinkedIn<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->Nirmal Kumar<!----><span class="white-space-pre"> </span>on LinkedIn<!----></span>

<!----></div>
          </div>
          <div class="display-flex ">
    <div class="display-flex full-width">
    
      
  <div class="pv-shared-text-with-see-more text-body-small break-words display-flex align-items-center">
    <div class="inline-show-more-text
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed
    inline-show-more-text--is-collapsed-with-line-clamp
    
    
    " style="line-height:1.9rem;max-height:11.399999999999999rem;-webkit-line-clamp:6;">

    <span aria-hidden="true"><!---->In last week’s post, we had seen 5 ways in which bosses get rid of us, their subordinates. The post had become a bit depressing and we had decided to break it up! Here we are again, with 5 more techniques of getting the bad news: 6. The Royal Seat This is similar to the ‘Bench’ in IT companies! You have completed your project. There were some hiccups. But now it is done and lessons learnt. As a compensation for the good work done on the project, you have been given a new role. This is a role recently created! Your responsibilities will be informed in due course. Meanwhile, you are free to do anything that interests you! You are overjoyed! You remind your boss the next day. He is busy. The day after, he is traveling. You wait for a week. The role has still not been defined. You realize you have been conned! The boss is back in office after a week. You type out your resignation and go to meet the boss. He is sad to know that you wish to resign. The company had great plans for you. Maybe you have identified some better prospects elsewhere. He accepts your resignation, reluctantly! 7. The Kick: Upstairs I have seen this happen in some state run organizations! Congratulations! In view of your good performance over the years you have been promoted. From now on you will be occupying the cabin of a Vice President. It is just next to the corner office. You can shift your belongings to your new office at your convenience. The boss sends an email and prints out an office order which the assistant pins on the Notice Board. You are the new Vice President in charge of Air-Conditioning! 8. The Kick: Downstairs This is a bit rare, but nasty! As a top manager, you have done a great job doubling the business of the company in the last year. You have traveled extensively, opened up virgin regions, established new offices, recruited new regional heads and set up the marketing practice. The Regional Heads report to you. Business is slow in some areas but growing fast in others. In fact so fast, that some of the new territories need expert attention. The management congratulates you and proposes that you would be the right person to head one of the fastest growing regions. You will take over from one of your direct reports and focus your energies in developing this promising territory. Are you willing to take up the challenge? 9. The Raft This appears to be a recent strategy! You are on a project. Apparently, things are going well. The client seems satisfied. He is still using the old technology. You feel he would be better off shifting to the more recent one, but he does not agree. They have already invested heavily into the old one. Your boss calls you. He is happy to inform you that you have been given a new project: one which works on the new technology. You will be the scrum master. You are happy. This is something you have been waiting for. A week later, the boss calls you in and informs that your performance on the new project is not up to the mark. You need to shift to another project. There are opportunities at other locations. The boss will let you know the options. You are shocked! Nothing of consequence has happened on the new project in the week. How did the boss come to that conclusion? Later on the grape vine tells you that the client in your previous project has some reservations about the progress made in the last couple of months! You had been put on a raft. And then they wanted it back! You are now at sea! 10. The Outsourced Shoulder You have recently joined the company. The new boss gives you a project and creates a team for you. You go through the names of your team members and find one which you are not too happy about. You had observed that person slacking, making excuses and gossiping in the office yesterday. You had made a snap judgment: you would be better off without that person. You inform the boss. The boss agrees to change the list. The next day, that person whom you had excluded, comes to you bitter and angry. You wonder why. The boss had asked that person to leave. The reason: you had given a negative report about that person’s attitude! You realize you have been used. The gun had always been pointing at that person. The boss was waiting for the right opportunity. And then thankfully, you came along with your broad shoulders! Now you will know a technique when you see one! Work to your fullest potential but beware of the ways of the boss! (The author is the Founder and Principal Consultant at ELM Consultancy and can be reached at nirmal@elmconsultancy.com. ELM Consultancy specializes in providing insights and solutions for individuals and employees to promote Excellence in Leadership and Management (ELM). www.elmconsultancy.com To subscribe to his blog please click http://www.elmconsultancy.com/subscribe-to-blog.html)<!----></span><span class="visually-hidden"><!---->In last week’s post, we had seen 5 ways in which bosses get rid of us, their subordinates. The post had become a bit depressing and we had decided to break it up! Here we are again, with 5 more techniques of getting the bad news: 6. The Royal Seat This is similar to the ‘Bench’ in IT companies! You have completed your project. There were some hiccups. But now it is done and lessons learnt. As a compensation for the good work done on the project, you have been given a new role. This is a role recently created! Your responsibilities will be informed in due course. Meanwhile, you are free to do anything that interests you! You are overjoyed! You remind your boss the next day. He is busy. The day after, he is traveling. You wait for a week. The role has still not been defined. You realize you have been conned! The boss is back in office after a week. You type out your resignation and go to meet the boss. He is sad to know that you wish to resign. The company had great plans for you. Maybe you have identified some better prospects elsewhere. He accepts your resignation, reluctantly! 7. The Kick: Upstairs I have seen this happen in some state run organizations! Congratulations! In view of your good performance over the years you have been promoted. From now on you will be occupying the cabin of a Vice President. It is just next to the corner office. You can shift your belongings to your new office at your convenience. The boss sends an email and prints out an office order which the assistant pins on the Notice Board. You are the new Vice President in charge of Air-Conditioning! 8. The Kick: Downstairs This is a bit rare, but nasty! As a top manager, you have done a great job doubling the business of the company in the last year. You have traveled extensively, opened up virgin regions, established new offices, recruited new regional heads and set up the marketing practice. The Regional Heads report to you. Business is slow in some areas but growing fast in others. In fact so fast, that some of the new territories need expert attention. The management congratulates you and proposes that you would be the right person to head one of the fastest growing regions. You will take over from one of your direct reports and focus your energies in developing this promising territory. Are you willing to take up the challenge? 9. The Raft This appears to be a recent strategy! You are on a project. Apparently, things are going well. The client seems satisfied. He is still using the old technology. You feel he would be better off shifting to the more recent one, but he does not agree. They have already invested heavily into the old one. Your boss calls you. He is happy to inform you that you have been given a new project: one which works on the new technology. You will be the scrum master. You are happy. This is something you have been waiting for. A week later, the boss calls you in and informs that your performance on the new project is not up to the mark. You need to shift to another project. There are opportunities at other locations. The boss will let you know the options. You are shocked! Nothing of consequence has happened on the new project in the week. How did the boss come to that conclusion? Later on the grape vine tells you that the client in your previous project has some reservations about the progress made in the last couple of months! You had been put on a raft. And then they wanted it back! You are now at sea! 10. The Outsourced Shoulder You have recently joined the company. The new boss gives you a project and creates a team for you. You go through the names of your team members and find one which you are not too happy about. You had observed that person slacking, making excuses and gossiping in the office yesterday. You had made a snap judgment: you would be better off without that person. You inform the boss. The boss agrees to change the list. The next day, that person whom you had excluded, comes to you bitter and angry. You wonder why. The boss had asked that person to leave. The reason: you had given a negative report about that person’s attitude! You realize you have been used. The gun had always been pointing at that person. The boss was waiting for the right opportunity. And then thankfully, you came along with your broad shoulders! Now you will know a technique when you see one! Work to your fullest potential but beware of the ways of the boss! (The author is the Founder and Principal Consultant at ELM Consultancy and can be reached at nirmal@elmconsultancy.com. ELM Consultancy specializes in providing insights and solutions for individuals and employees to promote Excellence in Leadership and Management (ELM). www.elmconsultancy.com To subscribe to his blog please click http://www.elmconsultancy.com/subscribe-to-blog.html)<!----></span>

<!----></div>
  </div>

  
  </div>

</div>
      </div>
  </div>

  </a>
